the Capture class to be more consistent 19 with the rest of the video library The following constructors 2 Capture PApplet parent int width int height 21 Capture PApplet parent int width int height int rate 22 Capture PApplet parent String name int width int height 23 Capture PApplet parent String name int width int height int rate 24 have been changed to 25 Capture PApplet parent int width int height 26 Capture PApplet parent int width int height int rate 27 Capture PApplet parent int width int height String name 28 Capture PApplet parent int width int height String name int rate 29 This version is not particularly consistent 3 Capture PApplet parent int width int height int rate 31 though we ll be leaving it in because it was used so heavily 3233 The split method has been altered to avoid inconsistency In fact 34 it has split itself into two methods Har har har 35 split String s has been removed use splitTokens String s instead 36 split String s char c remains unchanged 37 split String s String delim is now splitTokens String s String delim 38 The new model is that split breaks a String into pieces given a single39 delmiter which can be a single character or many characters For instance 4 split Something BR in BR BR HTML BR 41 now produces the array Something in HTML 42 The split method breaks the String whenever it sees the delimiter 43 so a BR next to another BR produces an empty String 44 On the other hand splitTokens takes a list of possible delimiters 45 and will consume one or more of any of them For instance 46 splitTokens really messed up with commas 47 will produce the array really messed up with commas 48 Because any group of comma or space characters and in any order 49 will simply be consumed as a single break 5 51 The casting functions e g int float boolean and friends52 have now been streamlined a bit to only cover casts that actually53 make sense 5455 Blending modes have been finalized for 1 thanks to the help56 of Dave Bollinger who contributed code to complete the set 57 http dev processing org bugs show bug cgi id 132 58 See the reference for blend for more details Thanks Dave 596 The constant CENTER RADIUS is now simply RADIUS Both still work 61 but CENTER RADIUS should be avoided 6263 The constants for ENTER TAB et al are now char values 64 rather than ints 6566 The framerate method in the movie library has been renamed to 67 frameRate 6869 Addition from Tom Hulbert to add setDTR to the Serial library 7 71 Where possible more methods inside PApplet have been made static 72 This may break some library code the OCD library is one example 73 until it s updated for 125 We ll try to add a more informative74 error message about this in 126 757677 additions improvements 7879 Significant improvement to text and images in OpenGL mode 8 Now using mipmaps to interpolate large and small images 8182 The println method with arrays now prints the array indices next 83 to each element making it a bit more useful The print method84 no longer supports arrays since that was a bit silly 8586 Major rework of the open command This function behaves differently87 on each platform On Windows the parameters are sent to the Windows 88 shell via cmd c On Mac OS X the open command is used type 89 man open in Terminal app for documentation On Linux it first tries9 gnome open then kde open but if neither are available it sends the91 command to the shell without any alterations For Java users this 92 is not quite the same as Runtime exec because the shell command 93 is prepended The method exec String is a shortcut for 94 Runtime getRuntime exec String This function was also modified 95 for Mac OS X and Linux support and to better handle spaces in 96 command names 9798 textAlign now supports a second parameter that 6335336Lots of bug fixes and two new libraries 337338 features 33934 Michael Chang s Candy SVG Importer has been expanded significantly 341 and added as a core library We are grateful to Michael for his342 contribution to the project 343344 A simple XML library processing xml has been added It is based on345 NanoXML and requires documents to be very strictly formatted and346 doesn t support some XML features 347348 For both of these new libraries they are intentionally minimal 349 implementations A full XML library or a full SVG import export 35 library would be quite significant in size We think it s instead351 helpful to have libraries that can be included as part of an applet 352 meaning that they should be no larger than around 2 3 k If you 353 don t need the compact size you can use a larger XML library 354 or something like Apache s Batik to handle SVG import 355356 bug fixes 357358 Lots of work done to improve the formatting and also make the359 key combinations work more 28 September 2 6571572This is a major release It contains a million billion bug fixes 573as well as several API changes as we try to firm up the API for 1 574575 PLEASE READ ALL THESE NOTES CAREFULLY 576 YOUR CODE NEEDS TO BE UPDATED 577578If you don t want to update your code yet and are just trying to get579your coursework done you may want to stick with release 115 58 581 The reference has received major updates The contents of the FAQ582 have now been integrated into the reference The remaining page583 of the FAQ has more details about where everyone went 584 http processing org faq html585586 framerate is now called frameRate for better API consistency 587 It didn t make sense to have a frameCount variable and a framerate 588 method as its misshapen cousin 58959 The default frameRate is now 6 fps This will prevent some odd591 quirks with sketches running faster than they need to and throttling592 the resources of your machine To disable this you can set the 593 frameRate arbitrarily high 594595 beginShape has changed LINE LOOP and LINE STRIP have been 596 removed because they are redundant and not consistent with the 597 rest of the API beginShape POLYGON is no longer recommended 598 simply use beginShape with no parameters when drawing an599 irregular shape Code examples 6 6 1 OLD SYNTAX 6 2 beginShape POLYGON 6 3 call vertex several times6 4 endShape 6 56 6 NEW SYNTAX 6 7 beginShape 6 8 call vertex several times6 9 endShape CLOSE 61 611 endShape with the CLOSE parameter will make the stroke on your612 shape continue back to where the shape started This is the same613 way that POLYGON and LINE LOOP worked 614615 OLD SYNTAX 616 beginShape LINE STRIP 617 draw with vertex 618 endShape 61962 NEW SYNTAX 621 noFill 622 beginShape 623 draw with vertex 624 endShape 625626 In the above case noFill must be called and the CLOSE parameter 627 to endShape is not used because the last point should not come 628 back to meet the original point 62963 OLD SYNTAX 631 beginShape LINE LOOP 632 draw with vertex 633 endShape 634635 NEW SYNTAX 636 noFill 637 beginShape 638 draw with vertex 639 endShape CLOSE 64 641 For the LINE LOOP example endShape CLOSE is used to specify close the642 shape noFill must also be called so that the shape is not filled in 643644 The two main problems with the old API were 1 LINE LOOP was simply a 645 POLYGON with no fill setting this made for a strange inconsistency 646 2 there was no way to draw a non closed POLYGON shape 647648 Using beginShape POLYGON doesn t make much sense when you re drawing 649 a line so this is one more reason that beginShape with no parameters65 is recommended 651652 The single pixel blend methods have been removed they were 653 overkill Also the blend function that blends a color instead654 of image data is now called blendColor 655656 Along with blendColor a lerpColor method has been added 657 It works just like lerp but with colors 658659 writer and reader are now createWriter and createReader 66 These weren t really documented so the change doesn t officially661 count per se but maybe someone was using em 662663 toInt and toFloat are now parseInt and parseFloat 664 to change to JavaScript syntax Not sure if anyone was using these 665666 Text with the JAVA2D setting no longer uses native fonts by default 667 which means they ll be slower and uglier See the reference for668 textFont for details and how it can be addressed 66967 Threading has been modified signficantly Some of these changes 671 had to be undone at the last minute so further changes are coming 672 The changes will fix several strange InterruptedException problems 673674675 major changes to PGraphics and its subclasses 676677 The PGraphics classes have all been reworked and renamed 678679 PGraphics is an abstract class on which additional PGraphics68 subclasses can be built It is an abstract class and therefore681 cannot be invoked directly 682683 PGraphics2D P2D contains the former contents of PGraphics that 684 are specific to 2D rendering This will be P2D once it is complete 685686 PGraphics3D P3D formerly PGraphics3 remains mostly unchanged 687688 PGraphicsJava2D JAVA2D formerly PGraphics2 is the renderer 689 used when you call for size width height JAVA2D It remains 69 the default renderer when none is specified It is slower but 691 more accurate than the others 692693 PGraphicsOpenGL OPENGL is the new name for PGraphicsGL 694695 Do not use new PGraphics to create PGraphics objects 696 Instead use createGraphics which will properly handle connecting697 the new graphics object to its parent sketch and will enable save 698 to work properly See the reference for createGraphics 699 http processing org reference createGraphics html7 7 1 For the same reasons as above createImage width height format 7 2 should be used instead of new PImage when creating images 7 3 http processing org reference createImage html7 47 5 PImage objects default to ARGB instead of RGB format This is 7 6 helpful for using createImage or createGraphics to generate7 7 a transparent surface Be sure to use PNG or another format that7 8 supports alpha 7 971 beginFrame and endFrame are now beginDraw and endDraw 711 Use these around drawing commands to a PGraphics created by712 createGraphics The defaults method should not need not713 be called just beginDraw and endDraw 714 class=\"searchable\">\n        \n  <table class=\"code\"><thead><tr><th class=\"lineno\" title=\"Line numbers\">Line</th><th class=\"content\">\u00a0</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><th id=\"L1\"><a href=\"#L1\">1</a></th><td>caution: the beverage you're about to enjoy is extremely hot. this</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2\"><a href=\"#L2\">2</a></th><td>file is a list of changes between each release. this is not a general</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L3\"><a href=\"#L3\">3</a></th><td>reference of how to use processing, because the information for older</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L4\"><a href=\"#L4\">4</a></th><td>releases will be super crusty. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L5\"><a href=\"#L5\">5</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L6\"><a href=\"#L6\">6</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L7\"><a href=\"#L7\">7</a></th><td>. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L8\"><a href=\"#L8\">8</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L9\"><a href=\"#L9\">9</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L10\"><a href=\"#L10\">10</a></th><td>ABOUT REV 0125 - 15 July 2007</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L11\"><a href=\"#L11\">11</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L12\"><a href=\"#L12\">12</a></th><td>Enormous number of bug fixes and additions. Many thanks to ewjordan </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L13\"><a href=\"#L13\">13</a></th><td>and fjen, who also contributed fixes for this release.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L14\"><a href=\"#L14\">14</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L15\"><a href=\"#L15\">15</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L16\"><a href=\"#L16\">16</a></th><td>[ api changes ] </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L17\"><a href=\"#L17\">17</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L18\"><a href=\"#L18\">18</a></th><td>+ Changed the constructors for the Capture class to be more consistent </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L19\"><a href=\"#L19\">19</a></th><td>\u00a0 with the rest of the video library. The following constructors:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L20\"><a href=\"#L20\">20</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L21\"><a href=\"#L21\">21</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height, int rate)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L22\"><a href=\"#L22\">22</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, String name, int width, int height)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L23\"><a href=\"#L23\">23</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, String name, int width, int height, int rate)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L24\"><a href=\"#L24\">24</a></th><td>\u00a0 have been changed to:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L25\"><a href=\"#L25\">25</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L26\"><a href=\"#L26\">26</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height, int rate)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L27\"><a href=\"#L27\">27</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height, String name)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L28\"><a href=\"#L28\">28</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height, String name, int rate)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L29\"><a href=\"#L29\">29</a></th><td>\u00a0 This version is not particularly consistent:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L30\"><a href=\"#L30\">30</a></th><td>\u00a0 Capture(PApplet parent, int width, int height, int rate)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L31\"><a href=\"#L31\">31</a></th><td>\u00a0 though we'll be leaving it in because it was used so heavily.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L32\"><a href=\"#L32\">32</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L33\"><a href=\"#L33\">33</a></th><td>+ The split() method has been altered to avoid inconsistency. In fact,</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L34\"><a href=\"#L34\">34</a></th><td>\u00a0 it has split itself into two methods. Har har har.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L35\"><a href=\"#L35\">35</a></th><td>\u00a0 split(String s), has been removed, use splitTokens(String s) instead.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L36\"><a href=\"#L36\">36</a></th><td>\u00a0 split(String s, char c) remains unchanged.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L37\"><a href=\"#L37\">37</a></th><td>\u00a0 split(String s, String delim) is now splitTokens(String s, String delim)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L38\"><a href=\"#L38\">38</a></th><td>\u00a0 The new model is that split() breaks a String into pieces given a single</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L39\"><a href=\"#L39\">39</a></th><td>\u00a0 delmiter, which can be a single character or many characters. For instance,</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L40\"><a href=\"#L40\">40</a></th><td>\u00a0 split(\"Something&lt;BR&gt;in&lt;BR&gt;&lt;BR&gt;HTML.\", \"&lt;BR&gt;\") </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L41\"><a href=\"#L41\">41</a></th><td>\u00a0 now produces the array \"Something\", \"in\", \"\", \"HTML\". </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L42\"><a href=\"#L42\">42</a></th><td>\u00a0 The split() method breaks the String whenever it sees the delimiter, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L43\"><a href=\"#L43\">43</a></th><td>\u00a0 so a &lt;BR&gt; next to another &lt;BR&gt; produces an empty String. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L44\"><a href=\"#L44\">44</a></th><td>\u00a0 On the other hand, splitTokens() takes a list of possible delimiters, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L45\"><a href=\"#L45\">45</a></th><td>\u00a0 and will consume one or more of any of them. For instance:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L46\"><a href=\"#L46\">46</a></th><td>\u00a0 splitTokens(\"really, messed ,up with ,,, commas,\", \", \");</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L47\"><a href=\"#L47\">47</a></th><td>\u00a0 will produce the array \"really\", \"messed\", \"up\", \"with\", \"commas\".</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L48\"><a href=\"#L48\">48</a></th><td>\u00a0 Because any group of comma or space characters (and in any order) </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L49\"><a href=\"#L49\">49</a></th><td>\u00a0 will simply be consumed as a single break.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L50\"><a href=\"#L50\">50</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L51\"><a href=\"#L51\">51</a></th><td>+ The casting functions, e.g. int(), float() boolean(), and friends</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L52\"><a href=\"#L52\">52</a></th><td>\u00a0 have now been streamlined a bit to only cover casts that actually</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L53\"><a href=\"#L53\">53</a></th><td>\u00a0 make sense.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L54\"><a href=\"#L54\">54</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L55\"><a href=\"#L55\">55</a></th><td>+ Blending modes have been finalized for 1.0, thanks to the help</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L56\"><a href=\"#L56\">56</a></th><td>\u00a0 of Dave Bollinger, who contributed code to complete the set:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L57\"><a href=\"#L57\">57</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=132\u00a0 </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L58\"><a href=\"#L58\">58</a></th><td>\u00a0 See the reference for blend() for more details. Thanks Dave!</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L59\"><a href=\"#L59\">59</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L60\"><a href=\"#L60\">60</a></th><td>+ The constant CENTER_RADIUS is now simply RADIUS. Both still work, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L61\"><a href=\"#L61\">61</a></th><td>\u00a0 but CENTER_RADIUS should be avoided.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L62\"><a href=\"#L62\">62</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L63\"><a href=\"#L63\">63</a></th><td>+ The constants for ENTER, TAB, et al. are now char values, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L64\"><a href=\"#L64\">64</a></th><td>\u00a0 rather than ints.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L65\"><a href=\"#L65\">65</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L66\"><a href=\"#L66\">66</a></th><td>+ The framerate() method in the movie library has been renamed to </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L67\"><a href=\"#L67\">67</a></th><td>\u00a0 frameRate().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L68\"><a href=\"#L68\">68</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L69\"><a href=\"#L69\">69</a></th><td>+ Addition from Tom Hulbert to add setDTR() to the Serial library.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L70\"><a href=\"#L70\">70</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L71\"><a href=\"#L71\">71</a></th><td>+ Where possible, more methods inside PApplet have been made static.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L72\"><a href=\"#L72\">72</a></th><td>\u00a0 This may break some library code (the OCD library is one example)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L73\"><a href=\"#L73\">73</a></th><td>\u00a0 until it's updated for 0125. We'll try to add a more informative</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L74\"><a href=\"#L74\">74</a></th><td>\u00a0 error message about this in 0126.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L75\"><a href=\"#L75\">75</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L76\"><a href=\"#L76\">76</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L77\"><a href=\"#L77\">77</a></th><td>[ additions, improvements ]</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L78\"><a href=\"#L78\">78</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L79\"><a href=\"#L79\">79</a></th><td>+ Significant improvement to text and images in OpenGL mode. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L80\"><a href=\"#L80\">80</a></th><td>\u00a0 Now using mipmaps to interpolate large and small images.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L81\"><a href=\"#L81\">81</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L82\"><a href=\"#L82\">82</a></th><td>+ The println() method with arrays now prints the array indices next </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L83\"><a href=\"#L83\">83</a></th><td>\u00a0 to each element, making it a bit more useful. The print() method</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L84\"><a href=\"#L84\">84</a></th><td>\u00a0 no longer supports arrays, since that was a bit silly.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L85\"><a href=\"#L85\">85</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L86\"><a href=\"#L86\">86</a></th><td>+ Major rework of the open() command. This function behaves differently</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L87\"><a href=\"#L87\">87</a></th><td>\u00a0 on each platform. On Windows, the parameters are sent to the Windows </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L88\"><a href=\"#L88\">88</a></th><td>\u00a0 shell via \"cmd /c\". On Mac OS X, the \"open\" command is used (type </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L89\"><a href=\"#L89\">89</a></th><td>\u00a0 \"man open\" in Terminal.app for documentation). On Linux, it first tries</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L90\"><a href=\"#L90\">90</a></th><td>\u00a0 gnome-open, then kde-open, but if neither are available, it sends the</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L91\"><a href=\"#L91\">91</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0command to the shell without any alterations. For Java users, this </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L92\"><a href=\"#L92\">92</a></th><td>\u00a0 is not quite the same as Runtime.exec(), because the shell command </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L93\"><a href=\"#L93\">93</a></th><td>\u00a0 is prepended. The method exec(String[]) is a shortcut for </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L94\"><a href=\"#L94\">94</a></th><td>\u00a0 Runtime.getRuntime.exec(String[]). This function was also modified </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L95\"><a href=\"#L95\">95</a></th><td>\u00a0 for Mac OS X and Linux support, and to better handle spaces in </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L96\"><a href=\"#L96\">96</a></th><td>\u00a0 command names.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L97\"><a href=\"#L97\">97</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L98\"><a href=\"#L98\">98</a></th><td>+ textAlign() now supports a second parameter that handles vertical </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L99\"><a href=\"#L99\">99</a></th><td>\u00a0 alignment of text. The second parameter can be TOP, CENTER, and </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L100\"><a href=\"#L100\">100</a></th><td>\u00a0 BOTTOM. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L101\"><a href=\"#L101\">101</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L102\"><a href=\"#L102\">102</a></th><td>+ Added min() and max() for float and int arrays.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L103\"><a href=\"#L103\">103</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L104\"><a href=\"#L104\">104</a></th><td>+ At Casey's urging, the \"Color Picker\" is now called the </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L105\"><a href=\"#L105\">105</a></th><td>\u00a0 \"Color Selector\". </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L106\"><a href=\"#L106\">106</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L107\"><a href=\"#L107\">107</a></th><td>+ Fix up MovieMaker from Dan Shiffman, also add the library to </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L108\"><a href=\"#L108\">108</a></th><td>\u00a0 the reference pages.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L109\"><a href=\"#L109\">109</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L110\"><a href=\"#L110\">110</a></th><td>+ Re-architect SVG to properly inherit fill/stroke/etc from parents</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L111\"><a href=\"#L111\">111</a></th><td>\u00a0 &lt;g&gt; object can specify fill/stroke for everyone below</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L112\"><a href=\"#L112\">112</a></th><td>\u00a0 need to discern between having a fill specified and one not being present</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L113\"><a href=\"#L113\">113</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L114\"><a href=\"#L114\">114</a></th><td>+ Fix Find/Replace button placement, also add Replace &amp; Find Next option</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L115\"><a href=\"#L115\">115</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=68</td></tr><tr><th 2006</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L314\"><a href=\"#L314\">314</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L315\"><a href=\"#L315\">315</a></th><td>Bug fixes for regressions found in 0122.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L316\"><a href=\"#L316\">316</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L317\"><a href=\"#L317\">317</a></th><td>+ Fixed an issue where drawing inside setup() didn't work, and any</td></tr><tr><th We are grateful to Michael for his</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L342\"><a href=\"#L342\">342</a></th><td>\u00a0 contribution to the project. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L343\"><a href=\"#L343\">343</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L344\"><a href=\"#L344\">344</a></th><td>+ A simple XML library (processing.xml) has been added. It is based on</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L345\"><a href=\"#L345\">345</a></th><td>\u00a0 NanoXML, and requires documents to be very strictly formatted, and</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L346\"><a href=\"#L346\">346</a></th><td>\u00a0 doesn't support some XML features. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L347\"><a href=\"#L347\">347</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L348\"><a href=\"#L348\">348</a></th><td>+ For both of these new libraries, they are intentionally minimal </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L349\"><a href=\"#L349\">349</a></th><td>\u00a0 implementations. A full XML library or a full SVG import/export </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L350\"><a href=\"#L350\">350</a></th><td>\u00a0 library would be quite significant in size. We think it's instead</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L351\"><a href=\"#L351\">351</a></th><td>\u00a0 helpful to have libraries that can be included as part of an applet, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L352\"><a href=\"#L352\">352</a></th><td>\u00a0 meaning that they should be no larger than around 20-30k. If you </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L353\"><a href=\"#L353\">353</a></th><td>\u00a0 don't need the compact size, you can use a larger XML library, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L354\"><a href=\"#L354\">354</a></th><td>\u00a0 or something like Apache's Batik to handle SVG import.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L355\"><a href=\"#L355\">355</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L356\"><a href=\"#L356\">356</a></th><td>[ bug fixes ] </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L357\"><a href=\"#L357\">357</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L358\"><a href=\"#L358\">358</a></th><td>+ Lots of work done to improve the formatting, and also make the</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L359\"><a href=\"#L359\">359</a></th><td>\u00a0 key combinations work more appropriately for the various platforms.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L360\"><a href=\"#L360\">360</a></th><td>\u00a0 For instance, HOME and END keys now move to the beginning or end</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L361\"><a href=\"#L361\">361</a></th><td>\u00a0 of the document, while ctrl-left and right (cmd-left and right on mac) </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L362\"><a href=\"#L362\">362</a></th><td>\u00a0 moves to the beginning or the end of a line. Outdenting when a brace</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L363\"><a href=\"#L363\">363</a></th><td>\u00a0 is used and some other quirks have been ironed out more. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L364\"><a href=\"#L364\">364</a></th><td>\u00a0 Shift-backspace now also produces 'delete', which is a useful thing</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L365\"><a href=\"#L365\">365</a></th><td>\u00a0 found in many programming text editors. Also text selection and arrow </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L366\"><a href=\"#L366\">366</a></th><td>\u00a0 issues like http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=349</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L367\"><a href=\"#L367\">367</a></th><td>\u00a0 This is one of several fixes that improve the use of the arrow keys</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L368\"><a href=\"#L368\">368</a></th><td>\u00a0 along with cmd/alt-right/left and others. In general, the editor </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L369\"><a href=\"#L369\">369</a></th><td>\u00a0 has been mostly brought up to spec for how keys work. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L370\"><a href=\"#L370\">370</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L371\"><a href=\"#L371\">371</a></th><td>+ Fixed the menu shortcuts for next and previous tab:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L372\"><a href=\"#L372\">372</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=402</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L373\"><a href=\"#L373\">373</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L374\"><a href=\"#L374\">374</a></th><td>+ Fixed a problem where clicking the close box of Processing, then hitting</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L375\"><a href=\"#L375\">375</a></th><td>\u00a0 \"Cancel\" when asked to save changes, would close the window anyway.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L376\"><a href=\"#L376\">376</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=440</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L377\"><a href=\"#L377\">377</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L378\"><a href=\"#L378\">378</a></th><td>+ Changed \"Format for Discourse\" to \"Copy for Discourse\", which just </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L379\"><a href=\"#L379\">379</a></th><td>\u00a0 copies the code directly to the clipboard so it can easily be</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L380\"><a href=\"#L380\">380</a></th><td>\u00a0 pasted into the forum. ] </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L412\"><a href=\"#L412\">412</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L413\"><a href=\"#L413\">413</a></th><td>+ Printing a tab is now supported (but with caveats)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L414\"><a href=\"#L414\">414</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=27</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L415\"><a href=\"#L415\">415</a></th><td>\u00a0 The\"Page Setup\" dialog doesn't work very well because Java seems </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L416\"><a href=\"#L416\">416</a></th><td>\u00a0 to suck at printing, and sucks differently on different platforms:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L417\"><a href=\"#L417\">417</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=435</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L418\"><a href=\"#L418\">418</a></th><td>\u00a0 Also, only the current tab is printed:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L419\"><a href=\"#L419\">419</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=28</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L420\"><a href=\"#L420\">420</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L421\"><a href=\"#L421\">421</a></th><td>+ Added background() with alpha parameters, but only for use with </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L422\"><a href=\"#L422\">422</a></th><td>\u00a0 graphics created by createGraphics(). Also, it replaces the pixels</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L423\"><a href=\"#L423\">423</a></th><td>\u00a0 with pixels that have that alpha, it's not like drawing a semi-</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L424\"><a href=\"#L424\">424</a></th><td>\u00a0 transparent rect() onto the screen. Using</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L426\"><a href=\"#L426\">426</a></th><td>\u00a0 background(0, 0, 0, 128) will replace the background with black</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L427\"><a rect() for that.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L429\"><a href=\"#L429\">429</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L430\"><a href=\"#L430\">430</a></th><td>[ bug fixes ] </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L431\"><a . . . . . . . . . . . . . . </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L538\"><a href=\"#L538\">538</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L539\"><a href=\"#L539\">539</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L540\"><a href=\"#L540\">540</a></th><td>ABOUT REV 0118 - 1 October 2006</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L541\"><a href=\"#L541\">541</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L542\"><a href=\"#L542\">542</a></th><td>This release fixes two major bugs that are minor fixes. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L543\"><a href=\"#L543\">543</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L544\"><a href=\"#L544\">544</a></th><td>1. Repairs problems with exported applets that use the OpenGL library.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L545\"><a href=\"#L545\">545</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L546\"><a href=\"#L546\">546</a></th><td>2. Fixes an issue with size(w, h, PDF, \"blah.pdf\");</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L547\"><a href=\"#L547\">547</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L548\"><a href=\"#L548\">548</a></th><td>This version was re-released after the PDF bug was found in the midst</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L549\"><a href=\"#L549\">549</a></th><td>of posting the OpenGL fix. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L550\"><a href=\"#L550\">550</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L551\"><a href=\"#L551\">551</a></th><td>If this is the first release you're using since 0115 or earlier, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L552\"><a href=\"#L552\">552</a></th><td>please read the section below that contains the release notes for 0116. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L553\"><a href=\"#L553\">553</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L554\"><a href=\"#L554\">554</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L555\"><a href=\"#L555\">555</a></th><td>. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L556\"><a href=\"#L556\">556</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L557\"><a href=\"#L557\">557</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L558\"><a href=\"#L558\">558</a></th><td>ABOUT REV 0117 - 1 October 2006</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L559\"><a href=\"#L559\">559</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L560\"><a href=\"#L560\">560</a></th><td>This release fixes a problem with release 0116 that made exported</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L561\"><a href=\"#L561\">561</a></th><td>sketches much larger than necessary because extra files were included.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L562\"><a href=\"#L562\">562</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L563\"><a href=\"#L563\">563</a></th><td>If this is the first release you're using since 0115 or earlier, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L564\"><a href=\"#L564\">564</a></th><td>please read the section below that contains the release notes for 0116. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L565\"><a href=\"#L565\">565</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L566\"><a href=\"#L566\">566</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L567\"><a href=\"#L567\">567</a></th><td>. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L568\"><a href=\"#L568\">568</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L569\"><a href=\"#L569\">569</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L570\"><a href=\"#L570\">570</a></th><td>ABOUT REV 0116 - 28 September 2006</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L571\"><a href=\"#L571\">571</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L572\"><a href=\"#L572\">572</a></th><td>This is a major release. It contains a million billion bug fixes, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L573\"><a href=\"#L573\">573</a></th><td>as well as several API changes as we try to firm up the API for 1.0.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L574\"><a href=\"#L574\">574</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L575\"><a href=\"#L575\">575</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 *** PLEASE READ ALL THESE NOTES CAREFULLY ***</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L576\"><a href=\"#L576\">576</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 ***\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0YOUR CODE NEEDS TO BE UPDATED!\u00a0 \u00a0 ***</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L577\"><a href=\"#L577\">577</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L578\"><a href=\"#L578\">578</a></th><td>If you don't want to update your code yet, and are just trying to get</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L579\"><a href=\"#L579\">579</a></th><td>your coursework done, you may want to stick with release 0115.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L580\"><a href=\"#L580\">580</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L581\"><a href=\"#L581\">581</a></th><td>+ The reference has received major updates. The contents of the FAQ</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L582\"><a href=\"#L582\">582</a></th><td>\u00a0 have now been integrated into the reference. The remaining page</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L583\"><a href=\"#L583\">583</a></th><td>\u00a0 of the FAQ has more details about where everyone went:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L584\"><a href=\"#L584\">584</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://processing.org/faq.html</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L585\"><a href=\"#L585\">585</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L586\"><a href=\"#L586\">586</a></th><td>+ framerate() is now called frameRate(), for better API consistency.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L587\"><a href=\"#L587\">587</a></th><td>\u00a0 It didn't make sense to have a frameCount variable and a framerate()</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L588\"><a href=\"#L588\">588</a></th><td>\u00a0 method as its misshapen cousin. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L589\"><a href=\"#L589\">589</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L590\"><a href=\"#L590\">590</a></th><td>+ The default frameRate is now 60 fps. This will prevent some odd</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L591\"><a href=\"#L591\">591</a></th><td>\u00a0 quirks with sketches running faster than they need to and throttling</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L592\"><a href=\"#L592\">592</a></th><td>\u00a0 the resources of your machine. To disable this, you can set the </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L593\"><a href=\"#L593\">593</a></th><td>\u00a0 frameRate arbitrarily high.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L594\"><a href=\"#L594\">594</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L595\"><a href=\"#L595\">595</a></th><td>+ beginShape() has changed. LINE_LOOP and LINE_STRIP have been </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L596\"><a href=\"#L596\">596</a></th><td>\u00a0 removed because they are redundant, and not consistent with the </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L597\"><a href=\"#L597\">597</a></th><td>\u00a0 rest of the API. beginShape(POLYGON) is no longer recommended, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L598\"><a href=\"#L598\">598</a></th><td>\u00a0 simply use beginShape() with no parameters when drawing an</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L599\"><a href=\"#L599\">599</a></th><td>\u00a0 irregular shape. Code examples:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L600\"><a href=\"#L600\">600</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L601\"><a href=\"#L601\">601</a></th><td>\u00a0 OLD SYNTAX:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L602\"><a href=\"#L602\">602</a></th><td>\u00a0 beginShape(POLYGON);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L603\"><a href=\"#L603\">603</a></th><td>\u00a0 // call vertex() several times</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L604\"><a href=\"#L604\">604</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape()</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L605\"><a href=\"#L605\">605</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L606\"><a href=\"#L606\">606</a></th><td>\u00a0 NEW SYNTAX:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L607\"><a href=\"#L607\">607</a></th><td>\u00a0 beginShape();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L608\"><a href=\"#L608\">608</a></th><td>\u00a0 // call vertex() several times</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L609\"><a href=\"#L609\">609</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape(CLOSE);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L610\"><a href=\"#L610\">610</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L611\"><a href=\"#L611\">611</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape() with the CLOSE parameter will make the stroke on your</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L612\"><a href=\"#L612\">612</a></th><td>\u00a0 shape continue back to where the shape started. This is the same</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L613\"><a href=\"#L613\">613</a></th><td>\u00a0 way that POLYGON and LINE_LOOP worked.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L614\"><a href=\"#L614\">614</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L615\"><a href=\"#L615\">615</a></th><td>\u00a0 OLD_SYNTAX:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L616\"><a href=\"#L616\">616</a></th><td>\u00a0 beginShape(LINE_STRIP);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L617\"><a href=\"#L617\">617</a></th><td>\u00a0 // draw with vertex()</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L618\"><a href=\"#L618\">618</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L619\"><a href=\"#L619\">619</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L620\"><a href=\"#L620\">620</a></th><td>\u00a0 NEW SYNTAX:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L621\"><a href=\"#L621\">621</a></th><td>\u00a0 noFill();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L622\"><a href=\"#L622\">622</a></th><td>\u00a0 beginShape();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L623\"><a href=\"#L623\">623</a></th><td>\u00a0 // draw with vertex();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L624\"><a href=\"#L624\">624</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L625\"><a href=\"#L625\">625</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L626\"><a href=\"#L626\">626</a></th><td>\u00a0 In the above case, noFill() must be called, and the CLOSE parameter </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L627\"><a href=\"#L627\">627</a></th><td>\u00a0 to endShape() is not used, because the last point should not come </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L628\"><a href=\"#L628\">628</a></th><td>\u00a0 back to meet the original point.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L629\"><a href=\"#L629\">629</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L630\"><a href=\"#L630\">630</a></th><td>\u00a0 OLD SYNTAX:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L631\"><a href=\"#L631\">631</a></th><td>\u00a0 beginShape(LINE_LOOP);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L632\"><a href=\"#L632\">632</a></th><td>\u00a0 // draw with vertex()</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L633\"><a href=\"#L633\">633</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L634\"><a href=\"#L634\">634</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L635\"><a href=\"#L635\">635</a></th><td>\u00a0 NEW SYNTAX:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L636\"><a href=\"#L636\">636</a></th><td>\u00a0 noFill();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L637\"><a href=\"#L637\">637</a></th><td>\u00a0 beginShape();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L638\"><a href=\"#L638\">638</a></th><td>\u00a0 // draw with vertex();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L639\"><a href=\"#L639\">639</a></th><td>\u00a0 endShape(CLOSE);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L640\"><a href=\"#L640\">640</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L641\"><a href=\"#L641\">641</a></th><td>\u00a0 For the LINE_LOOP example, endShape(CLOSE) is used to specify close the</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L642\"><a href=\"#L642\">642</a></th><td>\u00a0 shape. noFill() must also be called, so that the shape is not filled in.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L643\"><a href=\"#L643\">643</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L644\"><a href=\"#L644\">644</a></th><td>\u00a0 The two main problems with the old API were 1) LINE_LOOP was simply a </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L645\"><a href=\"#L645\">645</a></th><td>\u00a0 POLYGON with no fill setting, this made for a strange inconsistency.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L646\"><a href=\"#L646\">646</a></th><td>\u00a0 2) there was no way to draw a non-closed POLYGON shape. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L647\"><a href=\"#L647\">647</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L648\"><a href=\"#L648\">648</a></th><td>\u00a0 Using beginShape(POLYGON) doesn't make much sense when you're drawing </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L649\"><a href=\"#L649\">649</a></th><td>\u00a0 a line, so this is one more reason that beginShape() with no parameters</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L650\"><a href=\"#L650\">650</a></th><td>\u00a0 is recommended.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L651\"><a href=\"#L651\">651</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L652\"><a href=\"#L652\">652</a></th><td>+ The single pixel blend() methods have been removed, they were </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L653\"><a href=\"#L653\">653</a></th><td>\u00a0 overkill. Also, the blend() function that blends a color, instead</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L654\"><a href=\"#L654\">654</a></th><td>\u00a0 of image data, is now called blendColor().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L655\"><a href=\"#L655\">655</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L656\"><a href=\"#L656\">656</a></th><td>+ Along with blendColor(), a lerpColor() method has been added.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L657\"><a href=\"#L657\">657</a></th><td>\u00a0 It works just like lerp()... but with colors!</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L658\"><a href=\"#L658\">658</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L659\"><a href=\"#L659\">659</a></th><td>+ writer() and reader() are now createWriter() and createReader().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L660\"><a href=\"#L660\">660</a></th><td>\u00a0 These weren't really documented, so the change doesn't officially</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L661\"><a href=\"#L661\">661</a></th><td>\u00a0 \"count\" per se, but maybe someone was using 'em.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L662\"><a href=\"#L662\">662</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L663\"><a href=\"#L663\">663</a></th><td>+ toInt() and toFloat() are now parseInt() and parseFloat(), </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L664\"><a href=\"#L664\">664</a></th><td>\u00a0 to change to JavaScript syntax. Not sure if anyone was using these.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L665\"><a href=\"#L665\">665</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L666\"><a href=\"#L666\">666</a></th><td>+ Text with the JAVA2D setting no longer uses native fonts by default,</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L667\"><a href=\"#L667\">667</a></th><td>\u00a0 which means they'll be slower and uglier. See the reference for</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L668\"><a href=\"#L668\">668</a></th><td>\u00a0 textFont() for details and how it can be addressed.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L669\"><a href=\"#L669\">669</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L670\"><a href=\"#L670\">670</a></th><td>+ Threading has been modified signficantly. Some of these changes </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L671\"><a href=\"#L671\">671</a></th><td>\u00a0 had to be undone at the last minute, so further changes are coming.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L672\"><a href=\"#L672\">672</a></th><td>\u00a0 The changes will fix several strange InterruptedException problems.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L673\"><a href=\"#L673\">673</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L674\"><a href=\"#L674\">674</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L675\"><a href=\"#L675\">675</a></th><td>[ major changes to PGraphics and its subclasses ] </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L676\"><a href=\"#L676\">676</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L677\"><a href=\"#L677\">677</a></th><td>+ The PGraphics classes have all been reworked and renamed.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L678\"><a href=\"#L678\">678</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L679\"><a href=\"#L679\">679</a></th><td>\u00a0 - PGraphics is an abstract class on which additional PGraphics</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L680\"><a href=\"#L680\">680</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 subclasses can be built. It is an abstract class, and therefore</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L681\"><a href=\"#L681\">681</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 cannot be invoked directly. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L682\"><a href=\"#L682\">682</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L683\"><a href=\"#L683\">683</a></th><td>\u00a0 - PGraphics2D (P2D) contains the former contents of PGraphics that </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L684\"><a href=\"#L684\">684</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 are specific to 2D rendering. This will be P2D once it is complete.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L685\"><a href=\"#L685\">685</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L686\"><a href=\"#L686\">686</a></th><td>\u00a0 - PGraphics3D (P3D), formerly PGraphics3, remains mostly unchanged.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L687\"><a href=\"#L687\">687</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L688\"><a href=\"#L688\">688</a></th><td>\u00a0 - PGraphicsJava2D (JAVA2D), formerly PGraphics2, is the renderer </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L689\"><a href=\"#L689\">689</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 used when you call for size(width, height, JAVA2D). It remains </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L690\"><a href=\"#L690\">690</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 the default renderer when none is specified. It is slower but </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L691\"><a href=\"#L691\">691</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 more accurate than the others.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L692\"><a href=\"#L692\">692</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L693\"><a href=\"#L693\">693</a></th><td>\u00a0 - PGraphicsOpenGL (OPENGL) is the new name for PGraphicsGL.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L694\"><a href=\"#L694\">694</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L695\"><a href=\"#L695\">695</a></th><td>+ Do not use \"new PGraphics\" to create PGraphics objects.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L696\"><a href=\"#L696\">696</a></th><td>\u00a0 Instead, use createGraphics(), which will properly handle connecting</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L697\"><a href=\"#L697\">697</a></th><td>\u00a0 the new graphics object to its parent sketch, and will enable save()</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L698\"><a href=\"#L698\">698</a></th><td>\u00a0 to work properly. See the reference for createGraphics:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L699\"><a href=\"#L699\">699</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://processing.org/reference/createGraphics_.html</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L700\"><a href=\"#L700\">700</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L701\"><a href=\"#L701\">701</a></th><td>+ For the same reasons as above, createImage(width, height, format) </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L702\"><a href=\"#L702\">702</a></th><td>\u00a0 should be used instead of \"new PImage\" when creating images:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L703\"><a href=\"#L703\">703</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://processing.org/reference/createImage_.html</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L704\"><a href=\"#L704\">704</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L705\"><a href=\"#L705\">705</a></th><td>+ PImage objects default to ARGB instead of RGB format. This is </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L706\"><a href=\"#L706\">706</a></th><td>\u00a0 helpful for using createImage() or createGraphics() to generate</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L707\"><a href=\"#L707\">707</a></th><td>\u00a0 a transparent surface. Be sure to use PNG or another format that</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L708\"><a href=\"#L708\">708</a></th><td>\u00a0 supports alpha.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L709\"><a href=\"#L709\">709</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L710\"><a href=\"#L710\">710</a></th><td>+ beginFrame() and endFrame() are now beginDraw() and endDraw(). </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L711\"><a href=\"#L711\">711</a></th><td>\u00a0 Use these around drawing commands to a PGraphics created by</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L712\"><a href=\"#L712\">712</a></th><td>\u00a0 createGraphics(). The defaults() method should not/need not</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L713\"><a href=\"#L713\">713</a></th><td>\u00a0 be called, just beginDraw() and endDraw().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L714\"><a href=\"#L714\">714</a></th><td>\u00a0 </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L715\"><a href=\"#L715\">715</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L716\"><a href=\"#L716\">716</a></th><td>[ other additions and enhancements ]</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L717\"><a href=\"#L717\">717</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L718\"><a href=\"#L718\">718</a></th><td>+ Added an option to Preferences that sets the available memory </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L719\"><a href=\"#L719\">719</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=233</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L720\"><a href=\"#L720\">720</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L721\"><a href=\"#L721\">721</a></th><td>+ Added a menu option to switch between tabs</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L722\"><a href=\"#L722\">722</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=55</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L723\"><a href=\"#L723\">723</a></th><td>\u00a0 however, there's a problem where it sometimes stops working:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L724\"><a href=\"#L724\">724</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=402</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L725\"><a href=\"#L725\">725</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L726\"><a href=\"#L726\">726</a></th><td>+ The OpenGL library has been updated to use the \"final\" release </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L727\"><a href=\"#L727\">727</a></th><td>\u00a0 of JOGL 1.0, released September 2006, rather than beta 4, found</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L728\"><a href=\"#L728\">728</a></th><td>\u00a0 in release 0115. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L729\"><a href=\"#L729\">729</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L730\"><a href=\"#L730\">730</a></th><td>+ The flag in PApplet.main() formerly called --present-stop-color </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L731\"><a href=\"#L731\">731</a></th><td>\u00a0 is now simply --stop-color. A flag named --hide-stop has also </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L732\"><a href=\"#L732\">732</a></th><td>\u00a0 been added, to prevent users from quitting out of a present mode </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L733\"><a href=\"#L733\">733</a></th><td>\u00a0 application. see the faq on details for capturing ESC as well.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L734\"><a href=\"#L734\">734</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1079\"><a href=\"#L1079\">1079</a></th><td>+ A DXF file exporter. Lines and triangles from P3D or OPENGL </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1080\"><a href=\"#L1080\">1080</a></th><td>\u00a0 rendering modes can be sent directly to a DXF file. More information</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1081\"><a href=\"#L1081\">1081</a></th><td>\u00a0 and an example can be found in the developer's reference:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1082\"><a href=\"#L1082\">1082</a></th><td>\u00a0 http://dev.processing.org/reference/everything/javadoc/processing/dxf/RawDXF.html</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1083\"><a href=\"#L1083\">1083</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1084\"><a href=\"#L1084\">1084</a></th><td>+ A color picker has been added to the Tools menu. Using the keyboard </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1085\"><a href=\"#L1085\">1085</a></th><td>\u00a0 shortcuts, you can copy/paste the values for the colors and paste </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1086\"><a href=\"#L1086\">1086</a></th><td>\u00a0 them into your program. (We didn't do any sort of auto-insert of</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1087\"><a href=\"#L1087\">1087</a></th><td>\u00a0 colorMode() or fill() or stroke() code cuz we couldn't decide on a </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1088\"><a href=\"#L1088\">1088</a></th><td>\u00a0 good way to do this.. your contributions welcome).</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1089\"><a href=\"#L1089\">1089</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1090\"><a href=\"#L1090\">1090</a></th><td>+ We've decided to include versions of image and textFont that take</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1091\"><a href=\"#L1091\">1091</a></th><td>\u00a0 a filename instead of requiring a call to loadImage(). This is less </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1092\"><a href=\"#L1092\">1092</a></th><td>\u00a0 efficient than using loadImage because there's no way to unload it </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1093\"><a href=\"#L1093\">1093</a></th><td>\u00a0 from memory, but it's useful for beginners.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1094\"><a href=\"#L1094\">1094</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1095\"><a href=\"#L1095\">1095</a></th><td>\u00a0 void image(String filename, float x, float y)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1096\"><a href=\"#L1096\">1096</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1097\"><a href=\"#L1097\">1097</a></th><td>\u00a0 void image(String filename, float x, float y, float c, float d)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1098\"><a href=\"#L1098\">1098</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1099\"><a href=\"#L1099\">1099</a></th><td>\u00a0 void image(String filename,</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1100\"><a href=\"#L1100\">1100</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0float a, float b, float c, float d,</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1101\"><a href=\"#L1101\">1101</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0int u1, int v1, int u2, int v2)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1102\"><a href=\"#L1102\">1102</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1103\"><a href=\"#L1103\">1103</a></th><td>\u00a0 void textFont(String filename)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1104\"><a href=\"#L1104\">1104</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1105\"><a href=\"#L1105\">1105</a></th><td>\u00a0 void textFont(String filename, float size)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1106\"><a href=\"#L1106\">1106</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1107\"><a href=\"#L1107\">1107</a></th><td>+ The discourse formatter tool posted to the discourse board by owd </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1108\"><a href=\"#L1108\">1108</a></th><td>\u00a0 has been added to the Tools menu. used to specify PDF rendering.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1228\"><a href=\"#L1228\">1228</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1229\"><a href=\"#L1229\">1229</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1230\"><a href=\"#L1230\">1230</a></th><td>. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1231\"><a href=\"#L1231\">1231</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1232\"><a href=\"#L1232\">1232</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1233\"><a href=\"#L1233\">1233</a></th><td>ABOUT REV 0100 - 13 January 2006</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1234\"><a href=\"#L1234\">1234</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1235\"><a href=\"#L1235\">1235</a></th><td>This is a pre-release of the PDF generating code. There will be a couple </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1236\"><a href=\"#L1236\">1236</a></th><td>other quick releases to follow in the coming days, and this shouldn't be</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1237\"><a href=\"#L1237\">1237</a></th><td>considered a \"stable\" release since it's not been tested heavily, but we</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1238\"><a href=\"#L1238\">1238</a></th><td>wanted to post it for the people who'd like to try it out.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1239\"><a href=\"#L1239\">1239</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1240\"><a href=\"#L1240\">1240</a></th><td>To use it the pdf library, select Sketch -&gt; Import Library -&gt; pdf. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1241\"><a href=\"#L1241\">1241</a></th><td>And then choose one of the following methods:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1242\"><a href=\"#L1242\">1242</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1243\"><a href=\"#L1243\">1243</a></th><td>+ to render everything out to a file:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1244\"><a href=\"#L1244\">1244</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1245\"><a href=\"#L1245\">1245</a></th><td>\u00a0 void setup() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1246\"><a href=\"#L1246\">1246</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 size(400, 400, PDF, \"filename.pdf\");</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1247\"><a href=\"#L1247\">1247</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1248\"><a href=\"#L1248\">1248</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1249\"><a href=\"#L1249\">1249</a></th><td>\u00a0 void draw() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1250\"><a href=\"#L1250\">1250</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 // draw something good here</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1251\"><a href=\"#L1251\">1251</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1252\"><a href=\"#L1252\">1252</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1253\"><a href=\"#L1253\">1253</a></th><td>\u00a0 void mousePressed() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1254\"><a href=\"#L1254\">1254</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 exit();\u00a0 // important!</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1255\"><a href=\"#L1255\">1255</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1256\"><a href=\"#L1256\">1256</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1257\"><a href=\"#L1257\">1257</a></th><td>\u00a0 this will create a sketch that draws only to a file. successive frames</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1258\"><a href=\"#L1258\">1258</a></th><td>\u00a0 will be drawn on top of one another. when you're finished, call exit(), </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1259\"><a href=\"#L1259\">1259</a></th><td>\u00a0 for instance, inside mousePressed() or a keyPressed() event.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1260\"><a href=\"#L1260\">1260</a></th><td>\u00a0 this will still open a window of size 400x400 but not draw into it. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1261\"><a href=\"#L1261\">1261</a></th><td>\u00a0 future releases won't open the window, since it doesn't work properly </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1262\"><a href=\"#L1262\">1262</a></th><td>\u00a0 with sizes larger than the screen size (as might often be the case when</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1263\"><a href=\"#L1263\">1263</a></th><td>\u00a0 rendering to a file).</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1264\"><a href=\"#L1264\">1264</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1265\"><a href=\"#L1265\">1265</a></th><td>+ if you want to record just a single frame, use beginRecord() and</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1266\"><a href=\"#L1266\">1266</a></th><td>\u00a0 endRecord() inside draw:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1267\"><a href=\"#L1267\">1267</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1268\"><a href=\"#L1268\">1268</a></th><td>\u00a0 void draw() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1269\"><a href=\"#L1269\">1269</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 beginRecord(PDF, \"frame-####.pdf\");</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1270\"><a href=\"#L1270\">1270</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 // your awesome drawing happens here. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1271\"><a href=\"#L1271\">1271</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 endRecord();\u00a0 // saves the file</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1272\"><a href=\"#L1272\">1272</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1273\"><a href=\"#L1273\">1273</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1274\"><a href=\"#L1274\">1274</a></th><td>\u00a0 this can also be triggered by a mouse press. the #### will cause a</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1275\"><a href=\"#L1275\">1275</a></th><td>\u00a0 four digit \"frame\" number to be inserted into the filename.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1276\"><a href=\"#L1276\">1276</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1277\"><a href=\"#L1277\">1277</a></th><td>+ if you want to record the entire thing to a file at the same time as </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1278\"><a href=\"#L1278\">1278</a></th><td>\u00a0 drawing to the screen (i.e. save out an interactive drawing), do this:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1279\"><a href=\"#L1279\">1279</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1280\"><a href=\"#L1280\">1280</a></th><td>\u00a0 void setup() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1281\"><a href=\"#L1281\">1281</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 size(400, 400);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1282\"><a href=\"#L1282\">1282</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 // etc</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1283\"><a href=\"#L1283\">1283</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 beginRecord(PDF, \"everything.pdf\");</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1284\"><a href=\"#L1284\">1284</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1285\"><a href=\"#L1285\">1285</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1286\"><a href=\"#L1286\">1286</a></th><td>\u00a0 void draw() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1287\"><a href=\"#L1287\">1287</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 // do your worst</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1288\"><a href=\"#L1288\">1288</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1289\"><a href=\"#L1289\">1289</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1290\"><a href=\"#L1290\">1290</a></th><td>\u00a0 // this needn't be mousePressed, but you need to call this somewhere</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1291\"><a href=\"#L1291\">1291</a></th><td>\u00a0 // when you're done, to ensure that the pdf file properly closes.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1292\"><a href=\"#L1292\">1292</a></th><td>\u00a0 void mousePressed() {</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1293\"><a href=\"#L1293\">1293</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 endRecord();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1294\"><a href=\"#L1294\">1294</a></th><td>\u00a0 }</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1295\"><a href=\"#L1295\">1295</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1296\"><a href=\"#L1296\">1296</a></th><td>Caveats with PDF rendering: </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1297\"><a href=\"#L1297\">1297</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1298\"><a href=\"#L1298\">1298</a></th><td>+ anything bitmapped works very poorly. so it's no good for images.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1299\"><a href=\"#L1299\">1299</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1300\"><a href=\"#L1300\">1300</a></th><td>+ use createFont() with a truetype font (some opentype also work) to</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1301\"><a href=\"#L1301\">1301</a></th><td>\u00a0 make fonts work properly. any font that shows up in PFont.list() </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1302\"><a href=\"#L1302\">1302</a></th><td>\u00a0 should work. if you don't use createFont(), they'll likely show up </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1303\"><a href=\"#L1303\">1303</a></th><td>\u00a0 bitmappy and gross like images. the shape of the characters may be </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1304\"><a href=\"#L1304\">1304</a></th><td>\u00a0 weird in some cases, there seems to be a java bug with cubic vs. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1305\"><a href=\"#L1305\">1305</a></th><td>\u00a0 quadric splines. looking into a workaround if necessary. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1306\"><a href=\"#L1306\">1306</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1307\"><a href=\"#L1307\">1307</a></th><td>+ rendering from 3D isn't yet supported, but coming soon. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1308\"><a href=\"#L1308\">1308</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1309\"><a href=\"#L1309\">1309</a></th><td>+ exit() is really important when using PDF with size()</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1310\"><a href=\"#L1310\">1310</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1311\"><a href=\"#L1311\">1311</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1312\"><a href=\"#L1312\">1312</a></th><td>. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1313\"><a href=\"#L1313\">1313</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1314\"><a href=\"#L1314\">1314</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1315\"><a href=\"#L1315\">1315</a></th><td>ABOUT REV 0099 - 18 December 2005</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1316\"><a href=\"#L1316\">1316</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1317\"><a href=\"#L1317\">1317</a></th><td>A general usability-oriented release. The most major thing is some</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1318\"><a href=\"#L1318\">1318</a></th><td>additional support for auto-indenting of blocks (things inside curly</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L1319\"><a href=\"#L1319\">1319</a></th><td>braces) and being smarter about indents on new lines. the filter() stuff in PImage now works:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2338\"><a href=\"#L2338\">2338</a></th><td>\u00a0 + filter(GRAY) will convert a PImage to grayscale. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2339\"><a href=\"#L2339\">2339</a></th><td>\u00a0 + filter(INVERT) will invert an image</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2340\"><a href=\"#L2340\">2340</a></th><td>\u00a0 + filter(POSTERIZE, int levels) will posterize to that many levels</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2341\"><a href=\"#L2341\">2341</a></th><td>\u00a0 + filter(THRESHOLD) or filter(THRESHOLD, float midpoint)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2342\"><a href=\"#L2342\">2342</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 will give you a black and white image, with optionally settable</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2343\"><a href=\"#L2343\">2343</a></th><td>\u00a0 \u00a0 midpoint (a value from 0 to 1)</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2344\"><a href=\"#L2344\">2344</a></th><td>\u00a0 + coming soon is filter(BLUR) and filter(BLUR, float radius)...</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2345\"><a the font at its current size. the font api</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2351\"><a href=\"#L2351\">2351</a></th><td>\u00a0 built into PGraphics/PApplet now consists of:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2352\"><a href=\"#L2352\">2352</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2353\"><a href=\"#L2353\">2353</a></th><td>\u00a0 public void textFont(PFont which);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2354\"><a size);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2356\"><a href=\"#L2356\">2356</a></th><td>\u00a0 public void textLeading(float leading);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2357\"><a href=\"#L2357\">2357</a></th><td>\u00a0 public void textMode(int mode);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2358\"><a href=\"#L2358\">2358</a></th><td>\u00a0 public void textSpace(int space);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2359\"><a href=\"#L2359\">2359</a></th><td>\u00a0 public float textAscent();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2360\"><a href=\"#L2360\">2360</a></th><td>\u00a0 public float textDescent();</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2361\"><a href=\"#L2361\">2361</a></th><td>\u00a0 public float textWidth(char c);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2362\"><a href=\"#L2362\">2362</a></th><td>\u00a0 public float textWidth(String s);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2363\"><a href=\"#L2363\">2363</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2364\"><a href=\"#L2364\">2364</a></th><td>\u00a0 instead of using PFont.width() or PFont.ascent() to get the size of</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2365\"><a href=\"#L2365\">2365</a></th><td>\u00a0 text, you should use textWidth() or textAscent() in PGraphics/PApplet</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2366\"><a href=\"#L2366\">2366</a></th><td>\u00a0 which will return values based on what was set in textSize().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2367\"><a href=\"#L2367\">2367</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2368\"><a href=\"#L2368\">2368</a></th><td>- bezierVertex has changed. instead of four calls to bezierVertex, </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2369\"><a href=\"#L2369\">2369</a></th><td>\u00a0 you should instead use:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2370\"><a href=\"#L2370\">2370</a></th><td>\u00a0 vertex(x1, y1);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2371\"><a href=\"#L2371\">2371</a></th><td>\u00a0 bezierVertex(x2, y2, x3, y3, x4, y4);</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2372\"><a href=\"#L2372\">2372</a></th><td>\u00a0 this helps iron out some inconsistencies that you get with the wrong</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2373\"><a href=\"#L2373\">2373</a></th><td>\u00a0 number of bezierVertex coords. it also prevents you from having to </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2374\"><a href=\"#L2374\">2374</a></th><td>\u00a0 double up the final coordinate to draw the next segment.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2375\"><a href=\"#L2375\">2375</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2376\"><a href=\"#L2376\">2376</a></th><td>- got rid of CONCAVE_POLYGON and CONVEX_POLYGON since they never really</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2377\"><a href=\"#L2377\">2377</a></th><td>\u00a0 came into full use.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2378\"><a href=\"#L2378\">2378</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2379\"><a href=\"#L2379\">2379</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2380\"><a href=\"#L2380\">2380</a></th><td>bug fixes: </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2381\"><a href=\"#L2381\">2381</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2382\"><a href=\"#L2382\">2382</a></th><td>- curveVertex works again.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2383\"><a 1 March 2005</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2427\"><a href=\"#L2427\">2427</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2428\"><a href=\"#L2428\">2428</a></th><td>* PLEASE READ THIS INFORMATION BEFORE POSTING TO THE BETA LIST *</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2429\"><a href=\"#L2429\">2429</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2430\"><a href=\"#L2430\">2430</a></th><td>this is another release where processing has undergone href=\"#L2436\">2436</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2437\"><a href=\"#L2437\">2437</a></th><td>- whenever you use 3D in this release, you must use the depth() command</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2438\"><a href=\"#L2438\">2438</a></th><td>\u00a0 inside of setup (preferably just before or after size()). having</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2439\"><a href=\"#L2439\">2439</a></th><td>\u00a0 tried to keep the 2D rendering together, it's just become too messy</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2440\"><a href=\"#L2440\">2440</a></th><td>\u00a0 and error prone to continue. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2441\"><a href=\"#L2441\">2441</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2442\"><a href=\"#L2442\">2442</a></th><td>- after editing the pixels[] of an image, you must use the new method</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2443\"><a href=\"#L2443\">2443</a></th><td>\u00a0 updatePixels(). this became necessary because of the Java 2D</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2444\"><a href=\"#L2444\">2444</a></th><td>\u00a0 renderer as well as OpenGL. it's unfortunate, but it's all we can</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2445\"><a href=\"#L2445\">2445</a></th><td>\u00a0 do. so after messing with pixels[] for the main surface, or doing</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2446\"><a href=\"#L2446\">2446</a></th><td>\u00a0 the same with an image, call updatePixels() to mark the entire image</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2447\"><a href=\"#L2447\">2447</a></th><td>\u00a0 as modified, or call updatePixels(x, y, w, h) to update just a</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2448\"><a href=\"#L2448\">2448</a></th><td>\u00a0 portion (this is currently no faster, but later will represent an</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2449\"><a href=\"#L2449\">2449</a></th><td>\u00a0 optimization). </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2450\"><a href=\"#L2450\">2450</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2451\"><a href=\"#L2451\">2451</a></th><td>- you'll also need to use loadPixels() on any PGraphics object </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2452\"><a of some things significantly. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2524\"><a href=\"#L2524\">2524</a></th><td>\u00a0 for instance, using text on java 1.3 when depth() hasn't been called</td></tr><tr><th situation may require much more RAM. on the other hand, smoothed shapes</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2527\"><a href=\"#L2527\">2527</a></th><td>\u00a0 and general drawing in the same situation might be much faster.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2528\"><a href=\"#L2528\">2528</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2529\"><a href=\"#L2529\">2529</a></th><td>- i'm trying to think of a means to switch between the java 1.3 version </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2530\"><a href=\"#L2530\">2530</a></th><td>\u00a0 of the 2D api and the 1.1 version in case people want to force use of</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2531\"><a href=\"#L2531\">2531</a></th><td>\u00a0 the old one (once it's working again). we'll see.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2532\"><a href=\"#L2532\">2532</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2533\"><a href=\"#L2533\">2533</a></th><td>- presumably the separation of the rendering engines also means that</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2534\"><a href=\"#L2534\">2534</a></th><td>\u00a0 one could post a web applet that doesn't include the 3D rendering</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2535\"><a href=\"#L2535\">2535</a></th><td>\u00a0 code if your applet is only 2D (or vice versa).</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2536\"><a href=\"#L2536\">2536</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2537\"><a href=\"#L2537\">2537</a></th><td>- pmouseX and pmouseY have returned and are better than ever.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2538\"><a href=\"#L2538\">2538</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2539\"><a href=\"#L2539\">2539</a></th><td>- firstMouse boolean variable added, which is set 'true' when the</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2540\"><a href=\"#L2540\">2540</a></th><td>\u00a0 mouse gets its first legitimate mouse coordinate. naming for this</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2541\"><a href=\"#L2541\">2541</a></th><td>\u00a0 var will likely change in a future release.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2542\"><a href=\"#L2542\">2542</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2543\"><a href=\"#L2543\">2543</a></th><td>- arc() command has been added. it's just like ellipse:</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2544\"><a href=\"#L2544\">2544</a></th><td>\u00a0 arc(x, y, w, h, start, stop); </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2545\"><a href=\"#L2545\">2545</a></th><td>\u00a0 and uses ellipseMode() for its placement.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2546\"><a href=\"#L2546\">2546</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2547\"><a href=\"#L2547\">2547</a></th><td>- circle() has been removed. it was a dumb duplication with ellipse().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2548\"><a href=\"#L2548\">2548</a></th><td>\u00a0 it's not as though we have a square() function to go with rect().</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2549\"><a href=\"#L2549\">2549</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2550\"><a href=\"#L2550\">2550</a></th><td>- because of the separation of the 2D and 3D renderers, it should be</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2551\"><a href=\"#L2551\">2551</a></th><td>\u00a0 possible to create much larger PGraphics objects and for them to use</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2552\"><a href=\"#L2552\">2552</a></th><td>\u00a0 far less memory than before. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2553\"><a href=\"#L2553\">2553</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2554\"><a href=\"#L2554\">2554</a></th><td>- light() commands work, though things seem to look super ugly by</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2555\"><a href=\"#L2555\">2555</a></th><td>\u00a0 default. they're more correct when using OpenGL, and perhaps if</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2556\"><a href=\"#L2556\">2556</a></th><td>\u00a0 placed more explicitly, you may get better results.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2557\"><a href=\"#L2557\">2557</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2558\"><a href=\"#L2558\">2558</a></th><td>- the alpha() command that sets the alpha mask is now called</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2559\"><a functions. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2561\"><a href=\"#L2561\">2561</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2562\"><a href=\"#L2562\">2562</a></th><td>- imageMode(CORNER) and CORNERS are the only valid image modes. </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2563\"><a href=\"#L2563\">2563</a></th><td>\u00a0 imageMode affects get(), copy(), blend(), etc so it was just too</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2564\"><a href=\"#L2564\">2564</a></th><td>\u00a0 weird to have the CENTER functions operating in that mode. results</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2565\"><a href=\"#L2565\">2565</a></th><td>\u00a0 would have been very strange and unexpected.</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2566\"><a href=\"#L2566\">2566</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2567\"><a href=\"#L2567\">2567</a></th><td>- box() and sphere() should be working again with opengl</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2568\"><a href=\"#L2568\">2568</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2569\"><a href=\"#L2569\">2569</a></th><td>- die() is a newish internal function that's used whenever exceptions </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2570\"><a href=\"#L2570\">2570</a></th><td>\u00a0 or internal errors occur. you can make your own error handler by</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2571\"><a href=\"#L2571\">2571</a></th><td>\u00a0 overriding die(String s) and die(String s, Exception e) if you'd</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2572\"><a href=\"#L2572\">2572</a></th><td>\u00a0 like your applet to do something smarter than just halting. we're</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2573\"><a href=\"#L2573\">2573</a></th><td>\u00a0 moving to where exceptions and errors are handled in a more</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2574\"><a href=\"#L2574\">2574</a></th><td>\u00a0 consistent way, and that no p5 methods will require try and catch</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2575\"><a href=\"#L2575\">2575</a></th><td>\u00a0 style exception handling (for advanced users who want it, they can</td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2576\"><a href=\"#L2576\">2576</a></th><td>\u00a0 use the java equivalents of the various PApplet methods). </td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2577\"><a href=\"#L2577\">2577</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2578\"><a href=\"#L2578\">2578</a></th><td></td></tr><tr><th id=\"L2579\"><a
